## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics (materials science) — temperature-dependent constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which most naturally correspond to constitutive laws in mechanics of materials (elasticity, plasticity, viscoplastic/thermally activated flow, polymer hyperelasticity) where stiffness and strength depend on T and nonlinearly on epsilon.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelastic Hooke-type law: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (temperature-dependent modulus in small-strain elasticity)
- Additive thermal stress offset: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon (pre-stress/thermal mismatch plus elastic response)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial with T-dependent coefficients: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**2 (mild geometric/material nonlinearity)
- Power-law (Hollomon-type) hardening with thermal softening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 + c3 * T) * epsilon**c4 (plastic work hardening; parameters vary with T)
- Voce-type saturation hardening with T dependence: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 + c3 * T) * (1 - exp(-c4 * epsilon)) (approach to a saturation stress)
- Exponential temperature dependence of stiffness/flow stress: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (modulus or strength changing approximately exponentially with T over a range)
- Logarithmic hardening/activation form: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 + c3 * T) * log(c4 * epsilon + 1) (common empirical fit for gradual hardening)
- Johnson–Cook-like thermal softening (quasi-static variant): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - (c3 * T)**c4) (multiplicative temperature softening of strain hardening)
- Entropic (rubber-like) scaling with absolute temperature: sigma = (c0 * T) * (epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2) (polymer networks where stress scale ∝ T)
- Exponential stiffening (polymer/biomaterial-type): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (exp(c2 * epsilon) - 1) (rapid strain stiffening at larger epsilon)
- Elastic–plastic transition via smooth/hinge activation: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon - (c2 + c3 * T) * Max(epsilon - (c4 + c5 * T), 0) + c6 * Max(epsilon - (c4 + c5 * T), 0)**c7 (yield point then plastic hardening; yield strain shifts with T)
- Rational softening/stiffening with strain: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon / (1 + c2 * epsilon) + (c3 + c4 * T) * epsilon (captures initial linearity with gradual tangent-modulus change)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature-dependent modulus/strength → make coefficients multiplying epsilon or epsilon**n functions of T (e.g., c0 + c1*T, exp(c*T))
- Thermal softening often acts multiplicatively → sigma(epsilon,T) ≈ f(epsilon) * g(T) with g(T) decreasing like (1 - (c*T)**m) over a calibrated range
- Strain hardening without saturation → power laws in epsilon (epsilon**n) or log(c*epsilon+1) for gradual hardening
- Saturating hardening (finite asymptote) → use (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or related forms to cap the incremental hardening
- Yield/transition behavior with temperature shift → use Max(epsilon - epsilon_y(T), 0) or smooth approximations to represent elastic-to-plastic onset moving with T
- Polymer/entropic elasticity → include an overall factor proportional to T multiplying a strain function
- Rapid strain stiffening (e.g., polymers/biological tissues) → include exp(c*epsilon) terms for sharply increasing tangent modulus
- When initial linearity is required but tangent modulus decreases/increases with strain → use rational forms like epsilon/(1 + c*epsilon) added to or multiplied by T-dependent coefficients

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `83.23*epsilon^0.9685*exp(-93.02/(8.314*T)) + epsilon*4.14*sin(T - 349.02)`

The GT has two main terms:
1. **Arrhenius-like term:** `c0*epsilon^c1*exp(-c2/(c3*T))` — this involves `exp(-const/T)`
2. **Oscillatory term:** `epsilon*c4*sin(T - c5)` — this is `epsilon*sin(T + const)`

The key distinguishing feature is the `exp(-c2/(c3*T))` term. This is NOT equivalent to:
- A polynomial in T
- `T^c` (power law)
- `log(T)` or `T^(1/3)`
- `exp(c*T)` (exponential in T, not 1/T)
- `T*c0 + c1` (linear in T)
- Any rational function of T like `T/(aT+b)`

The `exp(-const/T)` function is a fundamentally different basis function. It cannot be replicated by polynomials, power laws, logarithms, or exponentials of T.

Let me check each candidate for whether it contains `exp(-const/T)` or something equivalent:

**Candidates 1-2, 17-19, 21, 23-24, 27, 29-32, 34, 36, 39, 45:** These contain terms with `epsilon` and `sin(T*c + c)` but NO exponential in T at all.
